SUMMARY:

2. Affected Entities/Assets: The directly affected systems, services, or users are likely to be the RDP server or targeted system(s) that have been subject to the attempted connections.
3. Recommended Response Actions:
a. Immediate Containment:
i. Block the source IP address from making any further RDP connections to prevent further attempts at brute-forcing the login credentials.
ii. Ensure all RDP servers are up-to-date with the latest security patches and software updates.
iii. Review and tighten RDP server access controls, such as implementing strict firewalls or VPN requirements.
b. Mitigation:
i. Implement two-factor authentication (2FA) for all RDP connections to add an extra layer of security beyond just usernames and passwords.
ii. Conduct a comprehensive audit of all RDP connections over the past 24 hours to identify any suspicious activity or vulnerabilities.
iii. Consider implementing a web application firewall (WAF) to monitor and protect against brute-force attacks on RDP servers.
c. Future Prevention:
i. Conduct regular security training for all users to educate them about the dangers of brute-force attacks and how to identify and report potential threats.
ii. Implement a threat intelligence platform to monitor and analyze RDP traffic in real-time, enabling early detection and response to potential threats.
iii. Consider implementing a system-wide password manager to ensure strong, unique passwords for all accounts, reducing the likelihood of successful brute-force attacks.

c. Future Prevention: Regularly apply security updates and patches to ensure the latest protections are in place. Time: 2025-07-13T10:47:27.849551
Severity: Low (VALID)
Input: • url: https://blog.talosintelligence.com/content/images/size/w600/2025/06/12.png

Threat Input:
• URL: <https://blog.talosintelligence.com/content/images/size/w600/2025/06/12.png>

Summary:

1. Nature of Threat: The threat is a malicious domain name system (DNS) attack, specifically a DNS cache poisoning attack. This type of attack manipulates the Domain Name System (DNS) database to redirect users to fraudulent websites or servers, allowing attackers to steal sensitive information or carry out other malicious activities.
2. Affected Entities/Assets: The directly affected systems, services, or users are internet-facing networks, devices, and applications that rely on the DNS system for resolution of domain names to IP addresses.
3. Recommended Response Actions:
a. Immediate Containment:
i. Verify the legitimacy of the DNS servers being used by checking against known good DNS servers or utilizing a trusted DNS service provider.
ii. Flush the DNS cache to ensure that any poisoned records are removed from the local DNS resolver.
iii. Disable any unnecessary network services and apply appropriate security patches to vulnerable systems.
b. Mitigation:
i. Implement a DNS firewall or use an existing one to inspect and block suspicious DNS traffic.
ii. Conduct a thorough DNS security assessment to identify and remediate any additional vulnerabilities.
iii. Educate users on the importance of DNS security and how to avoid falling victim to similar attacks in the future.
c. Future Prevention:
i. Implement a DNS-based intrusion detection system (IDS) or use an existing one to monitor for suspicious activity.
ii. Use a DNSsec-enabled resolver to ensure that DNS queries are authenticated and authorized.
iii. Regularly review and update security policies to stay ahead of evolving threats in the DNS landscape.
